     <p>
      <i>
       <b>
        Castle
       </b>
      </i>
      is an American crime drama television series, which premiered on
      <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">
       ABC
      </a>
      on March 9, 2009. The series is produced jointly by
      <a href="/wiki/Beacon_Pictures" title="Beacon Pictures">
       Beacon Pictures
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/ABC_Studios" title="ABC Studios">
       ABC Studios
      </a>
      . Created by
      <a href="/wiki/Andrew_W._Marlowe" title="Andrew W. Marlowe">
       Andrew W. Marlowe
      </a>
      , it primarily traces the lives of
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Castle" title="Richard Castle">
       Richard Castle
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Fillion" title="Nathan Fillion">
       Nathan Fillion
      </a>
      ), a best-selling mystery novelist, and
      <a href="/wiki/Kate_Beckett" title="Kate Beckett">
       Kate Beckett
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Stana_Katic" title="Stana Katic">
       Stana Katic
      </a>
      ), an NYPD homicide detective, as they solve various unusual crimes in New York City. Detective Beckett is initially infuriated at the thought of working with a writer and goes to great lengths to keep him out of her way. However, the two soon start developing feelings for each other. The overarching plot of the series focuses on the romance between the two lead characters, and the murder of Beckett's mother.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Premise">
       Premise
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Castle_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Premise">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      follows
      <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Fillion" title="Nathan Fillion">
       Nathan Fillion
      </a>
      as
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Castle" title="Richard Castle">
       Richard Castle
      </a>
      , a famous
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mystery_(fiction)" title="Mystery (fiction)">
       mystery novelist
      </a>
      who has killed off the main character in his book series and has
      <a href="/wiki/Writer%27s_block" title="Writer's block">
       writer's block
      </a>
      . He is brought in by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NYPD" title="NYPD">
       NYPD
      </a>
      for questioning regarding a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copycat_crimes" title="Copycat crimes">
       copy-cat murder
      </a>
      based on one of his novels. He is intrigued by this new window into crime and murder, and uses his connection with the mayor to charm his way into
      <a href="/wiki/Job_shadow" title="Job shadow">
       shadowing
      </a>
      Detective
      <a href="/wiki/Kate_Beckett" title="Kate Beckett">
       Kate Beckett
      </a>
      , played by
      <a href="/wiki/Stana_Katic" title="Stana Katic">
       Stana Katic
      </a>
      . Castle decides to use Beckett as the model for Nikki Heat, the main character of his next book series. Beckett, an avid reader of Castle's books, initially disapproves of having Castle shadow her work, but later warms up and recognizes Castle as a useful resource in her team's investigations.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cast_and_characters">
       Cast and characters
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Castle_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast and characters">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Castle_characters" title="List of Castle characters">
       List of Castle characters
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Main_cast">
       Main cast
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Castle_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Main cast">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Fillion" title="Nathan Fillion">
        Nathan Fillion
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Castle" title="Richard Castle">
        Richard Edgar Castle/Richard Alexander Rodgers
       </a>
       , a best-selling mystery writer. Plagued with
       <a href="/wiki/Writer%27s_block" title="Writer's block">
        writer's block
       </a>
       after killing off his popular lead character, Derrick Storm, whom he no longer found inspiring, Castle found himself involved in the case of a copycat killer recreating murder scenes from his novels. He discovers a new source of inspiration in Kate Beckett, the detective leading the investigation, so he uses his friendship with the mayor of New York to become involved in her investigations as a civilian consultant. He regularly uses his knowledge and talent to help solve murders, usually by taking evidence and assembling it into a narrative to explain their current case. He is twice-divorced and shares an apartment with his daughter and his mother. Earlier seasons of the show depict him as an immature womanizer; however, later seasons show a more mature and sensible side of him, albeit only slightly. His close working relationship with Beckett results in him falling in love with her. They get together in the start of season five. He proposes at the end of the fifth season, the two become engaged in season six, and they marry in the seventh season.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Stana_Katic" title="Stana Katic">
        Stana Katic
       </a>
       as Detective
       <a href="/wiki/Kate_Beckett" title="Kate Beckett">
        Katherine Houghton "Kate" Beckett
       </a>
       , a homicide detective with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NYPD" title="NYPD">
        NYPD
       </a>
       's 12th Precinct. Beckett is a first-class investigator who has gained a reputation for being intrigued by unusual cases. She joined the force after her mother was murdered in an unsolved case.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         1
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       After meeting Beckett, Castle is inspired to begin a new series of novels about a female NYPD detective named Nikki Heat, clearly based on Beckett. Initially cold and hard towards Castle, she soon warms up to him and eventually falls in love with him. In the fourth-season finale, Beckett resigns from the NYPD after she and Det. Esposito hide vital information regarding a case from Captain Gates, but later reneges on this and is allowed to return after she serves her suspension. She also briefly works as a Special Investigator for the Attorney General in early season six before returning to the NYPD. In the first episodes of season five, it becomes clear that Kate and Castle are in an
       <a href="/wiki/Intimate_relationship" title="Intimate relationship">
        intimate relationship
       </a>
       . The two become engaged at the start of the sixth season and get married in season seven.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Monet_Mazur" title="Monet Mazur">
        Monet Mazur
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Castle_characters#Gina_Cowell" title="List of Castle characters">
        Gina Cowell
       </a>
       , Castle's publisher and second ex-wife. Their personal relationship has been known to conflict with their professional one, with unfortunate results.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Jon_Huertas" title="Jon Huertas">
        Jon Huertas
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Javier_Esposito" title="Javier Esposito">
        Detective Javier "Javi"/"Espo" Esposito
       </a>
       , a former
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Special_Forces" title="United States Army Special Forces">
        Army Special Forces
       </a>
       soldier who now works in the homicide division as part of Beckett's team. He is always ready with a sardonic comment to keep Beckett on her toes and enjoys the way Castle riles her. He recognizes Castle's and Beckett's attraction from the start and sometimes advises Beckett on her relation to Castle. He and Kevin Ryan are close friends, even though they constantly argue about obscure facts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         2
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       He has a brief relationship with Dr. Lanie Parish in the third season, which ends with things being awkward between them, making them unable to work around each other for some time. He was suspended from the NYPD for hiding vital information from Captain Gates in a case concerning Beckett's well-being. In that case, he felt betrayed by his partner, Det. Kevin Ryan. He has since been reinstated on the force and has reconciled with Ryan.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Seamus_Dever" title="Seamus Dever">
        Seamus Dever
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kevin_Ryan_(Castle)" title="Kevin Ryan (Castle)">
        Detective Kevin Ryan
       </a>
       , a former Narcotics detective who also works as part of Beckett's team. He and Esposito regularly tease Beckett, but they are also protective of her.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         3
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The character was a late addition to the show as the original presentation pilot was only 37 minutes long.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         4
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Ryan marries his girlfriend, Jenny O'Malley, in season four. In the final episode of season four, Ryan fails to support Beckett and his partner Esposito, which jeopardizes his partnership with the two of them, although they reconcile later. In season five he is revealed to have worked undercover in the Irish mob. In season six, Jenny gives birth to their daughter.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Tamala_Jones" title="Tamala Jones">
        Tamala Jones
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lanie_Parish" title="Lanie Parish">
        Dr. Lanie Parish
       </a>
       , a medical examiner with an upbeat outlook. She is a friend of Beckett and is one of the few people Beckett can talk to easily and without reservation. Parish notices the personal connection between Beckett and Castle and urges her to act on it.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         5
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the third season, Lanie and Esposito begin a relationship they believe is secret, though the other main characters are aware of it. They later break up, making it awkward for them to work together for a time, but have since reconciled.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Ruben_Santiago-Hudson" title="Ruben Santiago-Hudson">
        Ruben Santiago-Hudson
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roy_Montgomery_(Castle)" title="Roy Montgomery (Castle)">
        Captain Roy Montgomery
       </a>
       (Season 13), Beckett's boss and Captain of the 12th Precinct. Montgomery appreciates Beckett's determination and diligence but maintains a close watch to make sure the investigations go smoothly. He is amused by how much Castle annoys Beckett but also appreciates how effectively the two work together. At the end of the third season, he is killed after staging a trap to capture a hired killer involved in the conspiracy that killed Beckett's mother.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         6
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the sixth-season episode "Veritas", Beckett recalls Montgomery's telling her, before she became a detective, to look through her mother's belongings for a clue in her murder. She finds a tape in which Bracken discusses the murder of Bob Armen and framing Joe Pulgatti, admitting to blackmailing the three cops over ransom money, intention to kill Johanna Beckett and admitting to previous murders.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Molly_Quinn" title="Molly Quinn">
        Molly Quinn
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexis_Castle" title="Alexis Castle">
        Alexis Castle
       </a>
       , Castle's teenaged daughter by his first wife, Meredith. Alexis is unusually intelligent for her age, and is often more mature and responsible than her father. She is very bright and enjoys school. A running gag in the series has her begging Castle to force her to study and do her homework instead of "fun" activities like parties and overnight trips. Her social and interpersonal issues often parallel some aspect of the case Castle and Beckett are investigating, and Castle sometimes asks her opinion on a killer's motivation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         7
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sullivan" title="Susan Sullivan">
        Susan Sullivan
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martha_Rodgers" title="Martha Rodgers">
        Martha Rodgers
       </a>
       , Castle's mother, an actress on and off Broadway. She lives with him and Alexis after an ex-husband has run off with her life savings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         8
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       She helps her son through the difficulties of raising a teenaged girl (even one as mature as Alexis) but also has an active social life of her own. She is free-spirited and often gives Castle valuable advice (which he seldom follows) regarding Beckett.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Penny_Johnson_Jerald" title="Penny Johnson Jerald">
        Penny Johnson Jerald
       </a>
       as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria_Gates" title="Victoria Gates">
        Captain Victoria Gates
       </a>
       (Season 4 ), Captain Montgomery's replacement. Formerly with Internal Affairs, Captain Gates (referred to by some as "Iron Gates") is more interested in career advancement and takes a dimmer view than her predecessor of the Beckett-Castle dynamic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JohnsonJerald_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-JohnsonJerald-9">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         9
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Strict and unforgiving, she loathes Castle's presence at the precinct, regarding him as an unprofessional, distracting and juvenile presence who interferes with the way she would prefer to run things. As the series progresses, she comes to tolerate Castle and even grudgingly accepts that he is useful for solving cases. Though her outright hostility fades, she is nonetheless strictly by the book, and still willing to beat Castle with it when needed. She is forced to remove Castle as an NYPD consultant when the DA's office learns about his friendship with a mob boss, but reinstates him after he rescues Beckett from Dr. Nieman and 3XK.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Toks_Olagundoye" title="Toks Olagundoye">
        Toks Olagundoye
       </a>
       as Hayley, a quick-witted, free-spirited former Scotland Yard police officer who works as a security specialist and isnt afraid to cross lines to get things done.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         10
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Recurring_characters">
       Recurring characters
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Castle_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Recurring characters">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Maya_Stojan" title="Maya Stojan">
        Maya Stojan
       </a>
       as Tory Ellis, an NYPD Tech officer who assists on Beckett's cases.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Arye_Gross" title="Arye Gross">
        Arye Gross
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Castle_characters#Sidney_Perlmutter" title="List of Castle characters">
        Dr. Sidney Perlmutter
       </a>
       , a medical examiner who assists on some of Beckett's cases and does little to hide his dislike of Castle.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Juliana_Dever" title="Juliana Dever">
        Juliana Dever
       </a>
       as Jenny O'Malley, Ryan's wife.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Trucco" title="Michael Trucco">
        Michael Trucco
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Castle_characters#Detective_Tom_Demming" title="List of Castle characters">
        Detective Tom Demming
       </a>
       , a handsome robbery detective with whom Beckett briefly becomes involved and whom Castle immediately dislikes.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Victor_Webster" title="Victor Webster">
        Victor Webster
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Castle_characters#Josh_Davidson" title="List of Castle characters">
        Dr. Josh Davidson
       </a>
       , Beckett's motorcycle-riding, cardiac-surgeon ex-boyfriend whom Castle repeatedly refers to as "motorcycle boy" and "doctor motorcycle boy".
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Ken_Baumann" title="Ken Baumann">
        Ken Baumann
       </a>
       as Ashley, Alexis' steady boyfriend. Alexis broke up with him after Castle and his mother were involved in a hostage situation and Ashley was nowhere to be found to help her through it.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Scott_Paulin" title="Scott Paulin">
        Scott Paulin
       </a>
       as Jim Beckett, Kate Beckett's father.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Bailey_Chase" title="Bailey Chase">
        Bailey Chase
       </a>
       as Will Sorenson, an FBI agent and Beckett's ex-boyfriend who wants to reconcile but immediately recognizes Beckett's attraction to Castle.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dorn" title="Michael Dorn">
        Michael Dorn
       </a>
       as Dr. Carver Burke, a psychiatrist who helps Beckett overcome her shooting and also deal with her various hidden emotions.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Pierson" title="Geoff Pierson">
        Geoff Pierson
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Castle_characters#Mr._Smith" title="List of Castle characters">
        Mr. Smith
       </a>
       , a friend of Captain Montgomery, who holds evidence that keeps the murderer of Beckett's mother away from Beckett; Smith occasionally acts through Castle to protect Beckett. He appeared to have been killed in "After the Storm," but in the episode "Veritas," it is revealed that he faked his death in order to operate in the shadows.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Darby_Stanchfield" title="Darby Stanchfield">
        Darby Stanchfield
       </a>
       as Meredith, an actress who was Castle's first wife and Alexis's mother. She is regularly portrayed as self-centered and dramatic.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Mosley_(actor)" title="Michael Mosley (actor)">
        Michael Mosley
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Castle_characters#Jerry_Tyson" title="List of Castle characters">
        Jerry Tyson/the Triple Killer (3XK)
       </a>
       , a methodical and meticulous serial killer who returns to New York every few years to terrorize the city. After being identified by Castle, Tyson turns his attentions to the 12th Precinct, variously targeting members of Beckett's team. He is shot and presumed to be dead in "Probable Cause" though Castle expresses doubts about it. It is suggested that he is still alive during the events of "Disciple", but the episode also explores the implications of his death, which leave Castle and Beckett disturbed.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Jack_Coleman_(actor)" title="Jack Coleman (actor)">
        Jack Coleman
       </a>
       as William Bracken, a popular and charismatic Senator representing the State of New York with ambitions of one day becoming President. He presents himself falsely as an honest man looking out for special interests, but is revealed in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castle_(season_5)" title="Castle (season 5)">
        season 5 premiere
       </a>
       to be highly corrupt and the person directly responsible for having Johanna Beckett murdered.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/James_Brolin" title="James Brolin">
        James Brolin
       </a>
       as a CIA deep-cover operative whose real name remains unknown; instead he has gone by aliases such as "Jackson Hunt" and "Anderson Cross." He is treated as a near-mythical figure in the intelligence community, and is revealed to be Castle's father in the two-part episode "Target" and "Hunt." Despite the loneliness of his profession, he has maintained indirect contact with his son.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Phil_LaMarr" title="Phil LaMarr">
        Phil LaMarr
       </a>
       as Dr. Holloway, a psychiatrist who evaluates the mental stability of suspects.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Myko Olivier as Pi, Alexis's boyfriend at the beginning of season 6, with whom she shares an apartment for a while (much to Castle's dismay.)
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Real-life writers
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_J._Cannell" title="Stephen J. Cannell">
       Stephen J. Cannell
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/James_Patterson" title="James Patterson">
       James Patterson
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Lehane" title="Dennis Lehane">
       Dennis Lehane
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Connelly" title="Michael Connelly">
       Michael Connelly
      </a>
      appear as themselves during periodic games of poker at Castle's apartment. Typically, they discuss Castle and Beckett's current case and tease Castle about his involvement with Beckett. On September 30, 2010, Cannell died in real life. The characters kept an empty chair at the poker table in his honor for a year.
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast_history">
       Broadcast history
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Castle_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Broadcast history">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      premiered as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midseason_replacement" title="Midseason replacement">
       midseason replacement
      </a>
      on ABC on March 9, 2009. ABC renewed
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      for a second season with an initial order of 13 episodes; ABC later extended the order to 22, then 24 episodes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The second season premiered on Monday, September 21, 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In March 2010, ABC renewed
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      for a third, 22-episode season, which began on September20, 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ewseason3_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ewseason3-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On November 11, 2010, ABC extended the episode order to 24.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4start_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-4start-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On January 10, 2011, ABC announced
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      had been renewed for a fourth season for 22episodes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Season four premiered on September 19, 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-futon-s4_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-futon-s4-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On December 8, 2011, ABC ordered an additional episode bringing season 4 up to 23 episodes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insidetv1_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-insidetv1-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On May 10, 2012,
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      was renewed for a fifth season by ABC,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-season5_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-season5-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which started on Monday September 24, 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Two additional episodes were ordered on October 19, 2012, and February 5, 2013, respectively. This brings season 5 up to a total of 24 episodes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On May 10, 2013, ABC announced via Twitter that
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      had been renewed for a sixth season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-s6renew_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-s6renew-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On May 8, 2014, ABC renewed the series for a seventh season,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which premiered on September 29, 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On May 7, 2015, the series was renewed for its eighth season.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The eighth season will premiere on September 21, 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>

     <p>
      The Season 2 episode "Boom!" (the finale of a two-part episode featuring
      <a href="/wiki/Dana_Delany" title="Dana Delany">
       Dana Delany
      </a>
      ) not only attracted the highest audience of the show's run (14.5 million viewers) but was also the highest-rated show on ABC in its time slot in 14years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ewseason3_14-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ewseason3-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Syndication">
       Syndication
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Castle_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Syndication">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In June 2011,
      <a href="/wiki/TNT_(TV_channel)" title="TNT (TV channel)">
       TNT
      </a>
      acquired exclusive cable rights from
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney-ABC_Domestic_Television" title="Disney-ABC Domestic Television">
       Disney-ABC Domestic Television
      </a>
      to air the first two seasons of
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      beginning in the summer of 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tnt_70-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-tnt-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In advance of the series' fourth season, TNT broadcast an eight-hour marathon of episodes on September 15, 2011, including five from season 3.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-season4_71-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-season4-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      began airing on TNT every Wednesday beginning September 26, 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      also began airing in broadcast syndication on weekends beginning September 29, 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tie-in_works">
       Tie-in works
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Castle_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tie-in works">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      In the series, Castle writes a novel titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Heat_Wave_(novel)" title="Heat Wave (novel)">
        Heat Wave
       </a>
       .
      </i>
      As a tie-in, ABC and sister publisher
      <a href="/wiki/Hyperion_Books" title="Hyperion Books">
       Hyperion Books
      </a>
      released that novel as a real book (
      <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781401323820">
       ISBN 978-1-4013-2382-0
      </a>
      ) with "Richard Castle" as the author. It is entirely in character from the dedication to the acknowledgments, although the latter mentions the principal cast and the show's creators by first name.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ABC released the first half of the novel in weekly increments on their website.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The complete novel was published in September 2009 as a hardcover, debuting at No. 26 on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Times_Best_Seller_list" title="New York Times Best Seller list">
       <i>
        The New York Times
       </i>
       Best Seller list
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In its fourth week on the list,
      <i>
       Heat Wave
      </i>
      broke into the top 10 at #6.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Heat Wave
      </i>
      was released in paperback (
      <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781401310400">
       ISBN 978-1-4013-1040-0
      </a>
      ) on July 27, 2010 and debuted at No. 34 on
      <i>
       The New York Times
      </i>
      bestseller Paperback Mass-Market list.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It once again appeared on
      <i>
       The New York Times
      </i>
      bestseller list on May 27, 2012 at #19.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naked_Heat" title="Naked Heat">
        Naked Heat
       </a>
      </i>
      (
      <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781401324025">
       ISBN 978-1-4013-2402-5
      </a>
      ), the sequel to
      <i>
       Heat Wave,
      </i>
      was released on September 28, 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Naked Heat
      </i>
      debuted at No. 7 on the New York Times Best Seller list.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As they did with
      <i>
       Heat Wave
      </i>
      , ABC released a series of the early chapters online as a promotional tool.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A third novel, titled
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikki_Heat" title="Nikki Heat">
        Heat Rises
       </a>
      </i>
      (
      <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781401324438">
       ISBN 978-1-4013-2443-8
      </a>
      ), was released on September 20, 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It debuted at No. 1 on
      <i>
       The New York Times
      </i>
      bestseller list on October 9, 2011
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and at No. 5 on the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USA_TODAY" title="USA TODAY">
        USA TODAY
       </a>
      </i>
      Best-Selling Books list.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The season three finale introduced a
      <a href="/wiki/Graphic_novel" title="Graphic novel">
       graphic novel
      </a>
      based on Castle's previous novel character, Derrick Storm.
      <i>
       Castle: Richard Castle's Deadly Storm
      </i>
      was published by
      <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">
       Marvel Comics
      </a>
      on September 28, 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It debuted at No. 3 on
      <i>
       The New York Times
      </i>
      bestseller list on October 16, 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A fourth novel, titled
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikki_Heat" title="Nikki Heat">
        Frozen Heat
       </a>
      </i>
      (
      <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781401324445">
       ISBN 978-1-4013-2444-5
      </a>
      ), was released on September 11, 2012,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and debuted on
      <i>
       The New York Times
      </i>
      bestseller list at No. 7 on September 23, 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The fifth Nikki Heat novel
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikki_Heat" title="Nikki Heat">
        Deadly Heat
       </a>
      </i>
      was released September 17, 2013 and debuted at No. 8 on the
      <i>
       New York Times
      </i>
      bestseller list.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       Raging Heat,
      </i>
      the sixth novel, was released on September 16, 2014. It landed on No. 6 on the
      <i>
       New York Times
      </i>
      Hardcover Fiction bestseller list
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and on No. 17 on
      <i>
       New York Times
      </i>
      Combined Print and E-Book Fiction bestseller list
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      on October 05, 2014.
     </p>
     <p>
      The seventh novel,
      <i>
       Driving Heat
      </i>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">

        <span>
         [
        </span>

        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      will be released on September 15, 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>

        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <p>
      In February 2012, Hyperion announced three e-book novellas to Richard Castle's famous Derrick Storm series. The first novella of the series,
      <i>
       A Brewing Storm
      </i>
      , was released in digital media on May 1, 2012. It debuted at No. 13 on
      <i>
       The New York Times
      </i>
      E-Book Fiction bestseller list,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as well as No. 18 on the
      <i>
       New York Times
      </i>
      Combine Prints &amp; E-book Fiction list
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      on May 20, 2012.
     </p>
     <p>
      On July 3, 2012, the second novella of the new Derrick Storm books,
      <i>
       A Raging Storm
      </i>
      , was released in e-book format. It landed on
      <i>
       The New York Times
      </i>
      bestseller e-books list at #19
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and at No. 31 for the combined Prints &amp; E-book list, both on July 22, 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The final Derrick Storm novella,
      <i>
       A Bloody Storm,
      </i>
      was released on August 7, 2012. It debuted on the
      <i>
       New York Times
      </i>
      bestseller e-books list at #20
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and at #34
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      on the combined Prints &amp; E-book list on August 26, 2012.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Derrick_Storm_television_series">
       Derrick Storm television series
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Castle_(TV_series)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Derrick Storm television series">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On August 20, 2014, ABC announced that the early development stage has begun on a television series centered on Derrick Storm. The series will be a CIA procedural written by
      <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Poirier" title="Gregory Poirier">
       Gregory Poirier
      </a>
      , who will executive-produce with
      <i>
       Castle
      </i>
      's Andrew Marlowe and Terri Miller.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
